<div id="review_1175447298" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175447298" />
    <a title="Kay (❦ ᴗ ❦ ✿) BooksandMe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35703415-kay-booksandme"><img alt="Kay (❦ ᴗ ❦ ✿) BooksandMe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514735804p2/35703415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175447298?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kay (❦ ᴗ ❦ ✿) BooksandMe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kay (❦ ᴗ ❦ ✿) BooksandMe" href="/user/show/35703415-kay-booksandme">Kay (❦ ᴗ ❦ ✿) BooksandMe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6610677-broken">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35703415-kay-booksandme?shelf=inspire-spirit">inspire-spirit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35703415-kay-booksandme?shelf=something-or-other">something-or-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35703415-kay-booksandme?shelf=books2015reads">books2015reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1175447298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10617009946397879399"><p>
  <br/>
</p><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>That the emotional infidelity was as real as if I’d gone to bed with him, and perhaps worse because merely sating a physical need was one thing but the inevitability of what was happening was something else, entirely.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This is completely different from what I have expected it should be. And then somehow, from the beginning, it takes me to a completely different perspective than what I have suspected in the first place. The struggle, and the ideas that this story presented is so muc</span>
  <span id="freeText10617009946397879399" style="display:none"><p>
  <br>
</p><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>That the emotional infidelity was as real as if I’d gone to bed with him, and perhaps worse because merely sating a physical need was one thing but the inevitability of what was happening was something else, entirely.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This is completely different from what I have expected it should be. And then somehow, from the beginning, it takes me to a completely different perspective than what I have suspected in the first place. The struggle, and the ideas that this story presented is so much so close to reality that I think on some point, it my taken a darker edge to what it is supposed to be.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443340298i/16350917.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The love that is in the story, somehow cannot be discern by a few sentences and paragraphs written. You have to immerse yourself in the overall situation and the difficulties that the main character has struggled with. I guess many readers would turn their backs on in reading this one because of the fact that this is so real and close to reality but me, I admired the struggle and how beautiful it is in the end.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>When did the fear go away, when would I stop longing, when would I cease wanting something that was wrong?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Sadie</b> is as much as brave as she is a coward. My mind only focused on her and the aspects of her life, her journey into something beautiful to only be shattered by an experience that completely changed her life. When faced with something like it, I’m sure you would also face the same thoughts she’d had. Her relief that he was alive, and so many ways, wished that he had died.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It’s just easier to keep doing the same thing. Play the same part, that’s all.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I think I like that I’ve never been into <b>Joe</b>’s head. The mystery that surrounds him keep it that way and that, I am thankful. His thoughts, his intentions, of why he kept to the first Friday of the month lunch meetings, why he did what he did, and everything else. I’ll never know and I’m not even curious. It’s what appeals him to me, actually.<br><br>Adam is Sadie’s husband. He has charmed me by how Sadie had described him how they’ve met. And after the incident that kept him completely crippled, he changed into a completely different person with only his pride left of him. His struggles of how he had become was all realistic, the thoughts he may had and the feelings he had to bottle up, his aggression and everything else in his life.<br><br>I’m actually torn of wanting Sadie to decide differently and yet, sometimes I want to push her in another direction at times. The things that she had to put up with left her completely broken.<br><br>The meetings with Joe were something I was excited and dreaded about. Excited that he will tell another story, and what difference that story from the last one and the others he had already told. How the Author managed to completely develop that character in such a way that I am completely engaged. And then dread, because of how it affects Sadie’s psyche and then I also became a different character each and every time.<br><br>The turn of events that leads up to the climax of the story and eventually the ending were unexpected. I didn’t know how Sadie will continue with her relationship and Joe had become something unexpected, what with not really being in his head, I don’t know how he would be acting or he will be there still. But I must say, I like how everything it turned out, not just because it ripped my heart out for Sadie and for everything that she had gone through, but on how it ended into something beautiful and open for possibilities. I must say <b>“the end is actually not the ending you expected it to be but a start to something beautiful”</b>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>It’s easier to keep being what you are, even if the only person who expects you to be it is yourself.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269844269?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4884889-mimi-smith?shelf=r">r</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269844269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16438014420002476875"><b>4 stars</b><br/><br/>This isn't a book-it's an emotional Roller Coaster. I went through every emotion in the book, while reading. I was happy, sad, angry, sympathetic, sad, you know *blushes*, and SAD again. If you're looking for something hot and sweet don't read it. If you're looking for heavy duty angst and real-life story then it might be. So, despite this book being classified as an Erotica, it's definitely not one to set you in the mood. Unless that mood is a depressed.<br/><br/><b>
  <u> The Premise</u>
</b><br/><br/>This book begins w</span>
  <span id="freeText16438014420002476875" style="display:none"><b>4 stars</b><br /><br />This isn't a book-it's an emotional Roller Coaster. I went through every emotion in the book, while reading. I was happy, sad, angry, sympathetic, sad, you know *blushes*, and SAD again. If you're looking for something hot and sweet don't read it. If you're looking for heavy duty angst and real-life story then it might be. So, despite this book being classified as an Erotica, it's definitely not one to set you in the mood. Unless that mood is a depressed.<br /><br /><b>
  <u> The Premise</u>
</b><br /><br />This book begins with the telling of a story we later learn Joe is telling to Sadie. It's a sexy story and we learn it's their ritual. Every first Friday of the month they would meet and talk. It might seem a budding romance...Until we find out Sadie is married. To Adam. The way the book is written, we gradually find out about Sadie's past and her current situation, about Adam, Joe, Sadie&amp;Adam, etc., in between Joe's monthly stories. It becomes clear Sadie and Adam are having marriage troubles, have been having them since Adam's accident when he became paralyzed. It has changed them and their marriage drastically and though love is still there, other, darker emotions are too. And while Sadie's situation with Joe isn't technically an affair, it's emotional cheating for sure.<br /><br />I'm still not sure whether I even <i>like</i> the plot and the characters, but I was absorbed by them all the same. Watching Sadie hurt Joe, Adam hurt Sadie, Sadie hurt Adam, Joe hurt Sadie was simply sad. The web of love, pain and lust was very present here. By the end I wasn't even sure how I wanted it to be resolved, I felt for them all. And while the ending was somewhat happy, more hopeful, it was, you guessed it, kind of sad too IMO.<br /><br />Here is a quote that was simply painful...<br /><br /><i>“Admit it,” Adam said finally, his voice cracked from screaming. “You wish I’d died.” <br />I got to my feet. Again, I got in his face, giving him the aggression he was giving me. He couldn’t shrink away. I think he wouldn’t have, even if he could. “Yes,” I told him. “Sometimes I wish you had.” <br />We stared at each other for what felt like a very long time. <br />“So do I,” Adam said.</i><br /><br />And two others that were hopeful...<br /><br /><i>"There are many things I don’t know, but quite a few I do. I know you can’t be lost if you know where you are. I know that life is full of precious and fragile things, and not all of them are pretty. I know that the sun follows the moon and makes days, one after another. Time passes. The world turns, and we turn with it, and though we can never go back to the beginning, sometimes, we can start again."<br /><br />"There is only one truth of which I feel confident, one thing I know that nothing else can change.<br />This month, my name is Sadie." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16438014420002476875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText2206776438568939413" style="display:none"><b> 1 star </b><br><br>CURIOSITY led me to read this book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529340245i/25814707.jpg" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> Before </b> - I've known this for years but have no plan on reading because the cover made me think of a pervert trying you molest a teen. (that was during my non reading of blurb days) <br><br><b> Now </b> - The blurb sounds interesting. And since some of my gr friends seemed to enjoy it, I decided to give it a go. <br><br><b> WRONG DECISION. </b><br><br>**** slightly spoilerish****<br><br>I know this is an erotica, but sex scenes already on chapter one? Okay, I'll take it. As the story progresses, I began to think what decent MARRIED woman will listen to a man she barely knew, talks about his sexcapades once every month? Even looks forward to their meeting as she envisions every single one of those scenes as her? - A person who is committing an emotional affair. <br><br>I hate Sadie for being so fake that she kept telling Adam she loves him when I, as a reader, don't see it. I see him more like a burden to her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ please... getting off while imaging other man? really? Mind you, she loves her husband.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The story also lacks character development. I hope that instead of those long descriptive one night stands and Elle's session - which in my <br>opinion, wasn't really necessary... Instead, it should focused more on character building. <br><br>The ONLY REASON why I continued to read on was because I accidentally read somewhere that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Adam wanted a divorce as he began to suspect that something was going on every first Friday of the month, since Sadie wears perfume. The expensive, special occasion stuff.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - pretty nice huh? that seems to be the only thing that kept me going on because I wanted to know how their relationship will turn out. <br><br>UNFORTUNATELY, INSTEAD of dealing with the complexity of the situation, the author decided <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the easy way out.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529340493ra/25814717.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everything after that just didn't make sense anymore. It felt like it was written by a different author. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Priscilla became a bitch, the relevance of the four some, and most of all the ending. <br><br><i> “From the first time you laughed with me, all those months, and all those stories,” Joe said quietly. “They were all you, to me. All of them were you.” </i> - call me stupid, but I cannot decipher this well.. does that mean every single woman he had sex with, he was thinking of Sadie? Even Priscilla? the woman he proposed to marrying? If so, he was sick and he just used all those woman. OR what it meant was he just made up all those stories? But then again, Priscilla is real !!?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Oh well, I don't want to dwell on it anymore because whatever it meant still wouldn't make me love this story. <br><br>As a matter of fact, this story pisses me off. Sorry.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_124917171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124917171" />
    <a title="Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn"><img alt="Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300839213p2/2310262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124917171?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quinn" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn">Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124917171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5578641565840948934">Wow. Just..... wow.<br/><br/><i>Broken</i> is an amazing book that defies description and categorization. It is not your typical erotica, nor can it be classed as romance, though it certainly contains elements of each. It is a complex and layered novel that is so much more than any synopsis could possibly represent.<br/><br/><i>Broken</i> is the story of three people - Sadie, her husband Adam, and Joe. But this is <b>not</b> a love triangle story.<br/><br/>Sadie and Adam meet in college and fall in love in the sweetest way. They marry and have t</span>
  <span id="freeText5578641565840948934" style="display:none">Wow. Just..... wow.<br /><br /><i>Broken</i> is an amazing book that defies description and categorization. It is not your typical erotica, nor can it be classed as romance, though it certainly contains elements of each. It is a complex and layered novel that is so much more than any synopsis could possibly represent.<br /><br /><i>Broken</i> is the story of three people - Sadie, her husband Adam, and Joe. But this is <b>not</b> a love triangle story.<br /><br />Sadie and Adam meet in college and fall in love in the sweetest way. They marry and have their whole lives to look forward to, until a tragedy shatters their existence and turns their entire world upside down in the most heartrending way.<br /><br />Sadie, desperately needing some relief from what has now become her existence, meets Joe. Strangers, they fall into an unspoken agreement that sees them meeting on the first Friday of every month. There, Joe will tell Sadie the story of his latest sexual encounter. Having had sexual intimacy in her marriage brutally taken away from her, Sadie imagines she is Joe's sexual partner in each story.<br /><br />Sadie remains desperately in love with her husband and, although she never cheats on him, is agonized that meeting with Joe is a form of emotional betrayal. For Sadie, life has become the ultimate no win situation.<br /><br /><i>Broken</i> is told in the first person from Sadie's point of view, and wouldn't be as powerful any other way. I didn't feel any of the limitations often found in first person narrative because the story is written in such a clever way.<br /><br />Even though Sadie was not present in any of the sexual encounters Joe describes, these are written in the first person from the female's point of view - a different character each time. We therefore get a different 'feel' each time. Joe, who begins as a complete stranger, also reveals more of himself in each encounter, so we get to know him at the same time as Sadie. The writing is so clever there is no way of knowing how much of the story comes from Joe, and how much from Sadie's imagination.<br /><br />There is a whole critical element in this novel that I have not included because I don't want to diminish the powerful impact on the reader.<br /><br /><i>Broken</i> is such an apt name for this novel. It is achingly sad, confronting and real - and different from anything I have ever read.<br /><br />I didn't find the sex gratuitous or kinky (although there is one f/f/f/m scene), but an integral part of the broader story, which is so much more than just the sum of these scenes.<br /><br /><i>Broken</i> will not be for everyone, but on the strength of this novel, I can see Megan Hart becoming one of my favorite authors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5578641565840948934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_42924470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42924470" />
    <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days"><img alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42924470?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=erotica">erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42924470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15864139157327184423">I started reading this book months ago, but after the first 70 pages or so found it too depressing to continue. Just the other day, though, Eastofoz read and loved it, and I was reminded I should just finish it. I picked it up again and the story just seemed to take off and turned out much better on the second attempt.<br/><br/>Sadie is a psychiatrist who spends all her time and energy caring for her quadriplegic husband, Adam, once a creative genius whom she met at uni. She's silent about the stress, fat</span>
  <span id="freeText15864139157327184423" style="display:none">I started reading this book months ago, but after the first 70 pages or so found it too depressing to continue. Just the other day, though, Eastofoz read and loved it, and I was reminded I should just finish it. I picked it up again and the story just seemed to take off and turned out much better on the second attempt.<br /><br />Sadie is a psychiatrist who spends all her time and energy caring for her quadriplegic husband, Adam, once a creative genius whom she met at uni. She's silent about the stress, fatigue and sheer burden she carries, listening to other people's problems but with no one to turn to herself. Her one indulgence is having lunch in the park with Joe on the first Friday of every month, when he tells her a new story for the month, about a new girl and what they did together.<br /><br />Sadie always imagines herself in the woman's place. Each month she's a different woman, being pleasured by Joe, who's tall, handsome, sexy, successful and a very good lover. He goes through women quickly, always holding himself back, never even kissing them as if it's too intimate an act, something he's saving for someone special. <br /><br />At home, things with Adam are worse than difficult. Sadie lives an isolated life, still in love with Adam but he's not even the same Adam she first fell in love with and married. Resentment, anger, even hatred rise up between them. And then, her one escape, those special days with Joe in the park, are ruined. Joe really does want to find the right woman, and now, almost as if to prove to Sadie that he can commit, he actually starts dating a cold, perfect investment banker. <br /><br />This is the difference between erotica and erotic romance: erotica can be heavy, sad, unsatisfying, self-indulgent even. I haven't read much of it, and what I have read has, at times, made me feel uneasy, disgusted, turned off, or bored. It's the romance that I love, and the intensity that comes with it, so erotic romance tends to be much more pleasurable, definitely more fun, certainly more satisfying to read. <br /><br />Sadie is a woman you can't help but pity. She has a crap life. Her guilt is understandable, her position undesirable. What would you do, in her place? How awful would it be? It seems almost ironic that she's a psychiatrist. Understanding doesn't make it any easier. She's stuck, and there doesn't seem to be any way out for her, and it's sad and depressing.<br /><br />Joe's another story. At first, I hated him. The first three monthly stories, the ones I read before putting the book aside, paint him as cold, aloof, distant, uncaring, all those things. And worst of all, you're getting everything through Sadie's eyes and thoughts: she wants nothing more than to be held, to be comforted, something Adam physically can't do, while here's Joe, throwing himself around, giving to all these women but never to Sadie. Her yearning and aching and loneliness made me feel bitter and angry.<br /><br />When I picked the book up again to give it another go, though, things subtly began to change. Sadie and Adam's situation isn't as predictable as you'd think, so I really didn't know what was going to happen and I like that. The best bit was Joe, though, whom we know and see through Sadie's first-person narration, but we see so much more than she does. She seems to shy away from really thinking about Joe, barely touching her feelings where he's concerned. Joe was more complicated than he seemed, and more worthwhile too. By the end, I sincerely cared for him and even though Sadie's decisions were perfectly realistic and understandable, I also felt terribly sorry for Joe.<br /><br />This isn't a romance, but it does have a happy ending, or the possibility of one, I'll give you that. If you want happy, stick to romance. Erotica's main concern is with delving into the human psyche and exploring it, and sex is a major part of that. You can't truly understand humans without understanding the sexual side of our natures. This I can appreciate, when it's done well, as it was here. The sadness, though: that's harder to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15864139157327184423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_71279954" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71279954" />
    <a title="Adrienne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2087365-adrienne"><img alt="Adrienne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71279954?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adrienne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adrienne" href="/user/show/2087365-adrienne">Adrienne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Adrienne by: </span>
      All other Megan Hart fans
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71279954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5816753026504396141">This book was everything I've come to expect from Megan Hart and more. So why is it so difficult for me to put into words exactly how I feel about it? I'm not going to write a re-word of the storyline as this has already been done, yet I feel I'm not doing any of the characters justice by not doing so.<br/><br/>What I want to make ia an observation of how I feel after reading this book. Sadie, Joe and Adam are products of a mind that understands human nature and can very eloquently inform,arouse and give </span>
  <span id="freeText5816753026504396141" style="display:none">This book was everything I've come to expect from Megan Hart and more. So why is it so difficult for me to put into words exactly how I feel about it? I'm not going to write a re-word of the storyline as this has already been done, yet I feel I'm not doing any of the characters justice by not doing so.<br /><br />What I want to make ia an observation of how I feel after reading this book. Sadie, Joe and Adam are products of a mind that understands human nature and can very eloquently inform,arouse and give hope all at the same time. This story has so much more going on than appears on the surface. Many aspects of human nature are played out,one thing for certain Megan Harts characters are not shallow by any means, even the ones who you think are, definately are not. So this book isn't just about Sadie, Joe and Adam but about all the other people we meet and their personalities too. I think this it what I liked so much, finding out and understanding what makes people tick, especially when faced with the loneliness of feeling unloved or uncared for, or when faced with something over which we have no control that alters our perception of another person on an emotional level. For me a compelling and erotic read, one which I shall,no doubt, re-visit. <br /><br />I think thats about all I have to say other than Megan Hart has said that she would like to write a story about Sarah the woman from Junes Story and I really hope she gets the opportunity to do so. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5816753026504396141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542682862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer506987687569486495">It's very atypical and unexpected erotic romance. It flows between hot and sexy (when reading about Joe's sexy escapades) to wholehearted and emotional story (when reading about Adam's accident and now his new way of life). Sadie connects this two lifes, lives fantasy life when listening to Joe's stories each first Friday every month and than lives real life with tetraplegic husband. Soon enough we realize Joe is much more than author shows us at the beginning. <br/><br/>It felt like two stories were merg</span>
  <span id="freeText506987687569486495" style="display:none">It's very atypical and unexpected erotic romance. It flows between hot and sexy (when reading about Joe's sexy escapades) to wholehearted and emotional story (when reading about Adam's accident and now his new way of life). Sadie connects this two lifes, lives fantasy life when listening to Joe's stories each first Friday every month and than lives real life with tetraplegic husband. Soon enough we realize Joe is much more than author shows us at the beginning. <br /><br />It felt like two stories were merged in one book, story isn't highly angst-ridden, but I loved writing style and amazingly described details. <br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N5UiRSrItc2GhedTJClKp92WnXc8MxeZiYcFzwApmbL4G2rWfEb5rUeGIcOdJAamy/wKDqN86wo+0XS8TFTgsA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pUbfovL1dwFCv1nil042tfeXWBHd//pIt/zJGJBbEJ5qyJcxpHs7YYO8n3IuQ3q04f3PaEKwBtsAqrhr3CZpnA==')})
  }
